<meta name="DC.Description" content="The halotolerant alga Dunaliella salina is a model for stress tolerance and is used commercially for production of beta-carotene (=pro-vitamin A). The presented draft genome of the genuine strain CCAP19/18 will allow investigations into metabolic processes involved in regulation of stress responses, including carotenogenesis and adaptations to life in high-salinity environments." />

<meta name="citation_title" content="Draft Nuclear Genome Sequence of the Halophilic and Beta-Carotene-Accumulating Green Alga Dunaliella salina Strain CCAP19/18" />
<meta name="citation_abstract" lang="en" content="&lt;h3&gt;ABSTRACT&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The halotolerant alga &lt;i&gt;Dunaliella salina&lt;/i&gt; is a model for stress tolerance and is used commercially for production of beta-carotene (=pro-vitamin A). The presented draft genome of the genuine strain CCAP19/18 will allow investigations into metabolic processes involved in regulation of stress responses, including carotenogenesis and adaptations to life in high-salinity environments.&lt;/p&gt;" />

<span class='nlm-sup'>c</span>

    <div class="item-list"><ul class="tabs inline panels-ajax-tab"><li class="first"><a href="/content/5/43/e01105-17" class="panels-ajax-tab-tab" data-panel-name="jnl_asm_tab_art" data-target-id="highwire_article_tabs" data-entity-context="node:8012" data-trigger="" data-url-enabled="1">Article</a><a href="/panels_ajax_tab/jnl_asm_tab_art/node:8012/1" rel="nofollow" style="display:none" class="js-crawler-link"></a></li><li><a href="/content/5/43/e01105-17/article-info" class="panels-ajax-tab-tab" data-panel-name="jnl_asm_tab_info" data-target-id="highwire_article_tabs" data-entity-context="node:8012" data-trigger="article-info" data-url-enabled="1">Info & Metrics</a><a href="/panels_ajax_tab/jnl_asm_tab_info/node:8012/1" rel="nofollow" style="display:none" class="js-crawler-link"></a></li><li class="last"><a href="/content/ga/5/43/e01105-17.full.pdf" class="panels-ajax-tab-tab" data-panel-name="jnl_asm_tab_pdf" data-target-id="highwire_article_tabs" data-entity-context="node:8012" data-trigger="full-text.pdf" data-url-enabled="1"><i class="icon-file-alt"></i> PDF</a><a href="/panels_ajax_tab/jnl_asm_tab_pdf/node:8012/1" rel="nofollow" style="display:none" class="js-crawler-link"></a></li></ul></div>  </div>

<div class="panel-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-highwire-panel-tabs-container" >
  
      
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <div data-panels-ajax-tab-preloaded="jnl_asm_tab_art" id="panels-ajax-tab-container-highwire_article_tabs" class="panels-ajax-tab-container"><div class="panels-ajax-tab-loading" style ="display:none"><img class="loading" src="https://mra.asm.org/sites/all/modules/contrib/panels_ajax_tab/images/loading.gif" alt="Loading" title="Loading" /></div><div class="panels-ajax-tab-wrap-jnl_asm_tab_art"><div class="panel-display panel-1col clearfix" >
  <div class="panel-panel panel-col">
    <div><div class="panel-pane pane-highwire-markup" >
  
      
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <div class="highwire-markup"><div xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml" id="content-block-markup" data-highwire-cite-ref-tooltip-instance="highwire_reflinks_tooltip" xmlns:xhtml="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"><div class="article fulltext-view "><span class="highwire-journal-article-marker-start"></span><div class="section abstract" id="abstract-1"><h2 class="">ABSTRACT</h2><p id="p-4">The halotolerant alga <em>Dunaliella salina</em> is a model for stress tolerance and is used commercially for production of beta-carotene (=pro-vitamin A). The presented draft genome of the genuine strain CCAP19/18 will allow investigations into metabolic processes involved in regulation of stress responses, including carotenogenesis and adaptations to life in high-salinity environments.</p></div><div class="section" id="sec-1"><h2 class="">GENOME ANNOUNCEMENT</h2><p id="p-5">The halotolerant green alga <em>Dunaliella salina</em> Teodoresco is the type species of the <em>Dunaliella</em> genus (class <em>Chlorophyceae</em>) (<a id="xref-ref-1-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-1">1</a>, <a id="xref-ref-2-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-2">2</a>). The biflagellate cells grow best at salinities of about 1.5 M (<a id="xref-ref-3-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-3">3</a>). Often, new isolates of halotolerant algae of this general appearance are incorrectly identified as <em>D. salina</em>. Strain CCAP 19/18 is a genuine representative of the species <em>D. salina</em> (<a id="xref-ref-4-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-4">4</a>), making it a reference for all ongoing and future studies on this and other <em>Dunaliella</em> species.</p><p id="p-6">Due to the absence of a rigid cell wall and the presence of a glycocalyx (<a id="xref-ref-5-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-5">5</a>), <em>D. salina</em> cells can adjust rapidly to large changes in salinity. Thus, <em>D. salina</em> is a model for studies of salinity tolerance (<a id="xref-ref-6-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-6">6</a><a id="xref-ref-7-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-7">–</a><a id="xref-ref-11-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-11">11</a>). Further, under abiotic stress cells turn orange due to overaccumulation of beta-carotene in plastidic oil globules (<a id="xref-ref-12-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-12">12</a>). Beta-carotene may accumulate to over 8% of the cellular dry weight, making the alga an important crop for the health food market for production of natural beta-carotene (<a id="xref-ref-13-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-13">13</a><a id="xref-ref-14-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-14">–</a><a id="xref-ref-17-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-17">17</a>). With the recent surge in <em>Dunaliella</em> “omics” research and currently 19 BioProjects deposited in NCBI (NIH), we offer this early release draft genome sequence of strain CCAP19/18 to support and encourage ongoing and future research.</p><p id="p-7">Following genomic DNA extraction from cells, libraries were generated for sequencing using either the Illumina or the PacBio platforms, overall producing 554.53 Gbp (after quality filtering). The tight-insert protocol was used for library construction for the Illumina HiSeq 2500 paired-end (PE) runs, which produced 219.9 Gbp (after quality filtering). For Illumina HiSeq 2000 sequencing preparation, the ligation-free paired end (LFPE) construction protocol was used for four libraries, the Illumina standard PE unamplified protocol was used for three libraries, and the Illumina CLIP PE protocol was used for one library, in total providing 341.6 Gbp (after quality filtering). Sequences generated on the Illumina platform provided 62× coverage and those from paired-end reads 27× (from 2-kb, 4-kb, and 6-kb libraries). Additionally, 16 PacBio single-molecule real-time (SMRT) libraries were constructed and sequenced on the PacBio RS platform, providing, after quality filtering, a total of 3.162 Gbp and resulting in about 10× coverage. The chloroplast and mitochondrial sequences (<a id="xref-ref-18-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-18">18</a>) were removed prior to assembly.</p><p id="p-8">The genome was assembled with ALLPATHS-LG (<a id="xref-ref-19-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-19">19</a>). The resulting assembly was scaffolded using SSPACE (<a id="xref-ref-20-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-20">20</a>) with three fosmid libraries (total of 0.50× read coverage). The final assembly was screened for contaminants against the NCBI nonredundant database. The <em>D. salina</em> v1.0 draft genome is provided through the Phytozome portal from the U.S. Department of Energy (DOE) Joint Genome Institute (JGI) at <a href="http://phytozome.jgi.doe.gov/">http://phytozome.jgi.doe.gov/</a>
. The main genome assembly provides approximately 343.7 Mb arranged in 5,512 scaffolds (<em>N</em><sub>50</sub> = 353.0 kbp) and a 49.1 G+C content. The contig <em>N</em><sub>50</sub> (<em>L</em><sub>50</sub>) = 10,635 (7.8 kb), and 1,241 scaffolds are &gt;50 kb in size, representing approximately 92.0% of the genome. With a conservative annotation approach using a repeat-masked assembly, the presented draft genome contains 16,697 loci providing 18,801 protein-coding transcripts. A less conservative annotation approach without masking repeats revealed 36,851 protein-coding genes. The assembly and annotation are expected to provide the foundation for future studies on halotolerance, secondary carotenoid accumulation, and algal stress biology.</p><div id="sec-2" class="subsection"><p id="p-9"><span class="inline-l2-heading">Accession number(s).</span>The whole-genome sequencing project was deposited in GenBank under BioProject number PRJNA32771. The project BioSample number is SAMN02746051 (sample name 1014865, SRA number SRS1543949). A trace file archive is available under NCBI project ID 32771. The draft genome sequence is accessible under GenBank accession number <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/NSFN00000000">NSFN00000000</a>
. This paper describes the first version, NSFN01000000.</p></div></div><div class="section ack" id="ack-1"><h2 class="">ACKNOWLEDGMENTS</h2><p id="p-10">The work conducted by the U.S. Department of Energy (DOE) Joint Genome Institute, a DOE Office of Science User Facility, is supported by the Office of Science of the U.S. Department of Energy under contract No. DE-AC02-05CH11231. This research was supported, in part, under the National Science Foundation Grants CNS-0958379, CNS-0855217, and ACI-1126113 and the City University of New York High Performance Computing Center at the College of Staten Island.</p></div><div class="section fn-group" id="fn-group-1"><h2>FOOTNOTES</h2><ul><ul class="history-list"><li xmlns:hwp="http://schema.highwire.org/Journal" class="received" hwp:start="2017-09-21"><span class="received-label">Received </span>21 September 2017.</li><li xmlns:hwp="http://schema.highwire.org/Journal" class="accepted" hwp:start="2017-09-25"><span class="accepted-label">Accepted </span>25 September 2017.</li><li class="published"><span class="published-label"> Published </span>26 October 2017.</li></ul></ul></div><ul class="copyright-statement"><li class="fn" id="copyright-statement-1">Copyright © 2017 Polle et al.</li></ul><div class="license" id="license-1"><p id="p-3">This is an open-access article distributed under the terms of the <a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/4.0/" rel="license">Creative Commons Attribution 4.0 International license</a>
.</p></div><div class="section ref-list" id="ref-list-1"><h2 class="">REFERENCES</h2><ol class="cit-list ref-use-labels"><li><span class="ref-label">1.</span><a class="rev-xref-ref" href="#xref-ref-1-1" title="View reference 1. in text" id="ref-1">↵</a><div class="cit ref-cit ref-journal" id="cit-5.43.e01105-17.1"><div class="cit-metadata"><ol class="cit-auth-list"><li><span
